    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText2834245056063911979" style="display:none">Gloria hasn’t had an easy life, she’s learned her lessons the hard way. She may have dressed flashy and dated a lot, but that’s in the past. Now she’s determined to change her reputation, and working along side the women in town as they prepare for the Christmas Pageant will give her a chance to prove she’s not a flirt. Small towns never forget, but will Smithville give her a second chance? <br /><br />Ned, the county Deputy, has his own secrets to keep. He’s heard the gossip about Gloria, but he sees all the kind things she does for the folks of Smithville. The upcoming Christmas Pageant will give him the opportunity to finally spend time with her, especially with his friends throwing them together, but can he overcome his frustrating stutter and talk to her, face to face? <br /><br />Fall in love with Ned and Gloria as all your favorite Smithville characters prepare for the Christmas Pageant, and get swept up into the most romantic Christmas Eve celebration ever!</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2598262989?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle&#39;s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle&#39;s" href="/user/show/37286206-danielle-s">Danielle&#39;s</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2598262989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5380708474707337420">Gloria is a beautiful woman. Unfortunately, she is also unlucky in love. She lives in the small town of Smithville, where everyone knows everyone and your social life is ripe gossip. <br/><br/>Gloria has dated most of the men in town and the local women have started to resent her. She has dated most of their husbands before they committed. Now she feels she shouldn’t dress nicely or go on any more dates. She feels her chance to find love has passed. She has low self-esteem and doesn’t want people to notic</span>
  <span id="freeText5380708474707337420" style="display:none">Gloria is a beautiful woman. Unfortunately, she is also unlucky in love. She lives in the small town of Smithville, where everyone knows everyone and your social life is ripe gossip. <br /><br />Gloria has dated most of the men in town and the local women have started to resent her. She has dated most of their husbands before they committed. Now she feels she shouldn’t dress nicely or go on any more dates. She feels her chance to find love has passed. She has low self-esteem and doesn’t want people to notice her. <br /><br />Ned is the local Deputy Sheriff. He finds Gloria in a state of sadness. Luckily it’s dark and he feels free to speak but his words don’t go down the way he hoped. Ned has a stutter and doesn’t feel he is good enough for someone as beautiful as Gloria. Ned is the local good boy and most people look up to him.<br /><br />These two form a sweet friendship in a time when they both need somebody. Christmas in Smithville is part of the Hometown series. It can easily be read as a standalone, however, these books are available in Kindle Unlimited. The town is small and the people love to medal. This is a sweet traditional Christmas tale. <br /><br />4 stars out of 5. I received an ARC as part of the blog tour, however, I read this book on Kindle Unlimited.</span>

<div id="review_2219405853" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2219405853" />
    <a title="J. W. Garrett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55979788-j-w-garrett"><img alt="J. W. Garrett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511906452p2/55979788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2219405853?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J. W. Garrett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J. W. Garrett" href="/user/show/55979788-j-w-garrett">J. W. Garrett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55979788-j-w-garrett?shelf=jaff-non">jaff-non</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55979788-j-w-garrett?shelf=era-modern-2">era-modern-2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55979788-j-w-garrett?shelf=source-arc">source-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55979788-j-w-garrett?shelf=holiday-christmas">holiday-christmas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55979788-j-w-garrett?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55979788-j-w-garrett?shelf=source-arc-netgalley">source-arc-netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2219405853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3511315884618255977">“A kiss is a secret which takes the lips for the ear.” Edmond Rostand, Cyrano de Bergerac<br/><br/>I would like to thank the publisher for this ARC [advanced reader copy] provided via Netgalley. <br/><br/>Book 1: Hometown Girl at Heart: Tara and Justin<br/>Book 2: Hometown Girl After All: Julia and Chad<br/>Book 3: Hometown Girl Forever: Lizzie and Elliot<br/><br/>After I started reading this… I discovered it was part 4 of the Hometown Series. That explained my feelings of “what the heck is going on” and solved my question of ‘did I m</span>
  <span id="freeText3511315884618255977" style="display:none">“A kiss is a secret which takes the lips for the ear.” Edmond Rostand, Cyrano de Bergerac<br /><br />I would like to thank the publisher for this ARC [advanced reader copy] provided via Netgalley. <br /><br />Book 1: Hometown Girl at Heart: Tara and Justin<br />Book 2: Hometown Girl After All: Julia and Chad<br />Book 3: Hometown Girl Forever: Lizzie and Elliot<br /><br />After I started reading this… I discovered it was part 4 of the Hometown Series. That explained my feelings of “what the heck is going on” and solved my question of ‘did I miss a book somewhere?’ Yeah, I did, three in fact. Having said that, in all fairness, it held fairly strong as a stand-a-lone. I just didn’t have the foundation and backstory to the many characters and friends of our main couple. However, the author did an excellent job in providing enough clues that I could enjoy the story and not worry about how these people became friends or how their relationships came about. <br /><br />I enjoyed the story; I liked the supporting characters and I was instantly drawn into the budding friendship and romance between our main couple. It had the feel of Cyrano de Bergerac in that our hero [Ned Knight] hid his identity so he could communicate with his lady interest. He spoke to her from the shadows, and sent her poetry… unsigned. The poor man was self-conscious about the defect in his speech… he stuttered when nervous. He felt that his speech imperfection disgusted women and he would not woo her because of it. Little did he know that women were drawn to his physical appearance and that negated any notice of his speech patterns. Poor man. <br /><br />Gloria, on the other hand, was dealing with her own set of problems. She felt the distrust and jealously from some of the women in the community as she tried to overcome the gossip regarding her shady past. She had determined to prove she had changed and declared that ‘she could do things without attracting male attention.’ Well, that may be a bit harder than she anticipated, short of no contact with men. <br /><br />Will our couple overcome their reluctance to step out and conquer their fears? Or will fear prevent their finding a lasting love?<br /><br />Rating: Clean. This story had so many references to other popular stories. It had the feel of ‘You’ve Got Mail,’ ‘Cinderella’ and her fairy godmother, Cyrano, and any of the miracle stories where good triumphs over evil or a pack of snarky women. Yeah, this was a feel-good Christmas story with a surprise ending that you will not believe. There were subtle clues, but I missed them completely. I had sort of an idea but this author took it to the extreme. Wow!! Just wow!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3511315884618255977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2218276926" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2218276926" />
    <a title="Alysha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62867742-alysha"><img alt="Alysha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518823685p2/62867742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2218276926?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alysha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alysha" href="/user/show/62867742-alysha">Alysha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2218276926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2791252267429731751">This book was a lovely snowy-day read! If you love watching Hallmark movies at Christmas, then you will definitely enjoy this book!<br/><br/>It starts off with Gloria, who has a bit of a reputation with men. She is trying to shake this image by devoting herself to charity work, making food for her neighbours, and dressing frumpy. Ned is the town’s deputy who has a bit stutter and a secret he is keeping from the town. The book is told from the point of view from both Gloria and Ned.<br/><br/>This was a feel-good rea</span>
  <span id="freeText2791252267429731751" style="display:none">This book was a lovely snowy-day read! If you love watching Hallmark movies at Christmas, then you will definitely enjoy this book!<br /><br />It starts off with Gloria, who has a bit of a reputation with men. She is trying to shake this image by devoting herself to charity work, making food for her neighbours, and dressing frumpy. Ned is the town’s deputy who has a bit stutter and a secret he is keeping from the town. The book is told from the point of view from both Gloria and Ned.<br /><br />This was a feel-good read. What I liked most of about this book intimacy of the characters. There is a short cast and it is easy to follow throughout the book. I would say my least favourite is the predictability; it’s a book about Christmas, a small town and an unlikely love story, and though it was predictable I would still recommend if you are looking for a good Christmas read.<br /><br />In exchange for an honest review, I received this book for free from NetGalley. This in no way affected my opinion of the book, or my review. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2791252267429731751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2250690183" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2250690183" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2250690183?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/8974343-laura">Laura</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2250690183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1376710166214205211">Small town America with characters that have real struggles makes this an interesting, albeit light read. <br/><br/>Smithville is set in somewhat rural Pennsylvania, less than an hour from the big city. Gloria is the gal who struggles to be accepted by the members of the community. Her boss and a few women have welcomed her with open arms while others are downright nasty to her.<br/><br/>She's volunteered to help with the upcoming Christmas pageant. Mutual friends notice a 'connection' or chemistry between her and </span>
  <span id="freeText1376710166214205211" style="display:none">Small town America with characters that have real struggles makes this an interesting, albeit light read. <br /><br />Smithville is set in somewhat rural Pennsylvania, less than an hour from the big city. Gloria is the gal who struggles to be accepted by the members of the community. Her boss and a few women have welcomed her with open arms while others are downright nasty to her.<br /><br />She's volunteered to help with the upcoming Christmas pageant. Mutual friends notice a 'connection' or chemistry between her and Ned, the Sherrif's Deputy. So, they do their best to push them together.<br /><br />In typical holiday romance style, Gloria and Ned become completely smitten with each other. However, can they move past their hang-ups and actually have a real relationship? <br /><br />Overall, this is a cute holiday time romance which makes for a great winter night read.<br /><br />Note ~ I received an ARC via NetGalley. All opinions are my own.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer344320600371167283"><strong>Wonderful Christmas Story</strong><br/><br/>First, I have to say that I was delighted to learn that this story takes place in Southwestern Pennsylvania, where I am from. And it's a small town romance--my favorite type of story. Gloria, who really has done nothing wrong, and has contributed to the community, is the victim of ugly gossip. But she has good friends who believe in her and stand by her, including deputy sheriff Ned. She has worked hard to prepare costumes for the Christmas pageant and avoid anything tha</span>
  <span id="freeText344320600371167283" style="display:none"><strong>Wonderful Christmas Story</strong><br /><br />First, I have to say that I was delighted to learn that this story takes place in Southwestern Pennsylvania, where I am from. And it's a small town romance--my favorite type of story. Gloria, who really has done nothing wrong, and has contributed to the community, is the victim of ugly gossip. But she has good friends who believe in her and stand by her, including deputy sheriff Ned. She has worked hard to prepare costumes for the Christmas pageant and avoid anything that could be considered flirting, to keep the gossipers at bay. It's Christmas eve before she realizes it. Feeling lonely and lost, all she wants to do is go home and go to bed. But here comes her Christmas surprise. Loved the story.</span>

I love the characters and the way the author switches between the perspectives of the two protagonists. Nothing like a small town at Christmas.<br/><br/>I've read all of Fullmer's books and I just love them! She is so great at providing the romance I crave in a book, but also presenting it in a very realistic way. I often find myself laughing out loud because of how much I can relate. </span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10792897540467467911" style="display:none">This story has everything you could want from it. You get a delightful romance, insight on Gloria, and cameos from all your favorite Smithville characters. If you haven't read the first three books you won't feel lost, but if you have you'll love seeing your favorite people weave in and out of each other's everyday life. I love Kirsten's stories because they are more of a character study than a romance. The plot line stands on it's own and the people are what make the books shine. The romance is just a wonderful bonus. They are clean, but not stuffy, fun. This is a great read and will get your heart in the Christmas Spirit!</span>

<div id="review_2206153521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2206153521" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6307294-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/images/nophoto/user/c_111x148.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2206153521?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/6307294-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6307294-maria?shelf=small-town">small-town</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6307294-maria?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6307294-maria?shelf=sexy-hero">sexy-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6307294-maria?shelf=mute-speech-probl">mute-speech-probl</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2206153521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2959268056206827662">"Received an Advance Reader Copy in exchange for a fair review"<br/>A quote:<br/>“She looked up, searching his face. He was very striking with his strong jaw, wavy mass of hair, and easy grin. His fine physique certainly didn’t hurt either. But he was Ned. The deputy. Solid and true; kind and thoughtful. And his stutter… she smiled at him, tenderness showing through. His tripped-up words were the thing that made him seem human, accessible”. (Quote from ARC)<br/><br/>This is a really entertaining book, with great ma</span>
  <span id="freeText2959268056206827662" style="display:none">"Received an Advance Reader Copy in exchange for a fair review"<br />A quote:<br />“She looked up, searching his face. He was very striking with his strong jaw, wavy mass of hair, and easy grin. His fine physique certainly didn’t hurt either. But he was Ned. The deputy. Solid and true; kind and thoughtful. And his stutter… she smiled at him, tenderness showing through. His tripped-up words were the thing that made him seem human, accessible”. (Quote from ARC)<br /><br />This is a really entertaining book, with great main characters and a cast of secondary characters that are complex and interesting too. I read it in one setting and found it delightful.<br />The hero, a small town deputy with a stutter, is really the highlight of the book. It’s incredibly sexy to read a hero who is both a law enforcement officer and has such an impediment. Ned is just adorable. The author, Kirsten Fullmer, really does a superb job in crafting the personality of Ned: his always alert persona as a deputy, his anxiety, shyness and fears because of his stutter, his sweetness and protectiveness and his hidden talents. All in all, Ned makes an alluring hero, with a mix of shyness (he even blushes) and resoluteness (he’s very convincing in his functions as a deputy). And, of course, who doesn’t fall in love with a man who is so good with babies (his interactions with baby Bella are delicious)?<br />The small town context was rather developed in the story. I had a little trouble understanding the women’s hostility towards the heroine, but that didn’t detract from the overall pleasure of reading the book.<br />I'm grateful to BooksGoSocial and NetGalley for providing a free copy <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2959268056206827662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Far fetched and at times, ridiculous.<br/><br/>I was given a copy of this book for free by Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2592153168&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2592153168" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2744047324723667721">Sometimes you can read a book in a series and not be at all lost. It is not the case with this book. If you just pick up this book without the rest of the series like I did, you will he running to catch up.<br/><br/>Gloria used to dress seductively and dated most of the guys in town. Which makes all the women hate her. Don't hate the ex. They are exes for a reason.<br/><br/>So Gloria dresses like a frump and does anonymous good deeds hoping the women of Smithville will get over it.<br/><br/>Ned the deputy stutters and thinks</span>
  <span id="freeText2744047324723667721" style="display:none">Sometimes you can read a book in a series and not be at all lost. It is not the case with this book. If you just pick up this book without the rest of the series like I did, you will he running to catch up.<br /><br />Gloria used to dress seductively and dated most of the guys in town. Which makes all the women hate her. Don't hate the ex. They are exes for a reason.<br /><br />So Gloria dresses like a frump and does anonymous good deeds hoping the women of Smithville will get over it.<br /><br />Ned the deputy stutters and thinks all the women of Smithville are laughing at his stutter but they actually think he's hot and think the stutter is adorable.<br /><br />The Chridtmas pageant throws Ned and Gloria together and they fall in love.<br /><br />So how does Ned tell her? Well Ned has a secret life in Pittsburgh. I spent the whole book thinking maybe his grandmother was dying in a hospice. No, he's secretly a singer with a big band orchestra. I have to admit, I didn't see that coming.<br /><br />I feel like the story took a sharp left turn when Nadine' s kindness makes her cry. I actually flipped back to make sure I didn't miss a page or a chapter.<br /><br />Anyway, Gloria and Ned are very sweet. Maybe someday I'll read the whole series and then be amazed at the things that happened in this one.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2223254652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2757964497406795781">I noticed both characters have their own insecurities; Ned with his speech disorder and Gloria with her lack of confidence. But I was more connected to Gloria’s character than Ned. Throughout the story, I watched how Gloria coped with her insecurity. How she learns to love herself before loving others. <br/>I love that Ned and her friends accepted her for what she is, a woman with a heart of gold despite her past. The friendship between each character was valuable in every way. In real life, it was d</span>
  <span id="freeText2757964497406795781" style="display:none">I noticed both characters have their own insecurities; Ned with his speech disorder and Gloria with her lack of confidence. But I was more connected to Gloria’s character than Ned. Throughout the story, I watched how Gloria coped with her insecurity. How she learns to love herself before loving others. <br />I love that Ned and her friends accepted her for what she is, a woman with a heart of gold despite her past. The friendship between each character was valuable in every way. In real life, it was difficult to find people who loved you as what you truly are. <br /><br />However, there was barely any descriptive explanation in regards to certain woman’s hostility towards Gloria other than what was mentioned in the paragraph. The pace of the story was slow but bearable as I could follow the building of Gloria’s character personality.  <br /><br />All in all, I truly enjoyed reading Christmas in Smithville. I would love to recommend this book to teen and adult readers who would love to read a cozy holiday clean romance book. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/3428010-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3428010-carolyn?shelf=clean-contemporary-romance">clean-contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3428010-carolyn?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2636476603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1192437009787867096">(3.5 stars)<br/><br/>Christmas in Smithville is a sweet, clean, cozy Christmas romance. Small-town, handsome cop with a stutter is paired with a generous, hard-working, former flirt.<br/><br/>The main characters were likable folks, and though I haven't read the other books in the series, I was able to follow the minor characters, who were all paired up.<br/><br/>The southwestern Pennsylvania setting was of interest to me since I grew up in that area and am familiar with both Pittsburgh and Uniontown. (I presume Smithville is</span>
  <span id="freeText1192437009787867096" style="display:none">(3.5 stars)<br /><br />Christmas in Smithville is a sweet, clean, cozy Christmas romance. Small-town, handsome cop with a stutter is paired with a generous, hard-working, former flirt.<br /><br />The main characters were likable folks, and though I haven't read the other books in the series, I was able to follow the minor characters, who were all paired up.<br /><br />The southwestern Pennsylvania setting was of interest to me since I grew up in that area and am familiar with both Pittsburgh and Uniontown. (I presume Smithville is fictional.)<br /><br />All in all, a likable story. The only thing that detracted from the book were the numerous grammatical errors and typos, which grew distracting (at least in the version of the book I read; it did not say it was an uncorrected proof). Misspellings and punctuation problems were the biggest offenders.<br /><br />I would've like to have seen the hero and heroine kiss at least once, but at least they got their happy ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1192437009787867096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Needed better editing.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+ItbHMTphqAzyb7wzxqcPBmmTJAZT+3StKzNq8krqPPCrTLOf7dPyJTiCpE475bjz/mrWNfCY7Xv0osaBGhaaQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ERkW+6k0qJDbfDGvTo2wbyRvoaJNedIGLJMUxTcpQJUrP38pEmph+HxXhc65eLqw8jBGaoP0XGF37VJ0+mqyDw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11248827457104066213">Kirsten is a writer with a love of art and design. She worked in the engineering field, taught college, and consulted free lance. Due to health problems, she retired in 2012 to travel with her husband. They live and work full time in a 40' travel trailer with their little dog Bingo. Besides writing romance novels, she enjoys selling art on Etsy and spoiling their three grandchildren. <br/><br/>As a writer, </span>
  <span id="freeText11248827457104066213" style="display:none">Kirsten is a writer with a love of art and design. She worked in the engineering field, taught college, and consulted free lance. Due to health problems, she retired in 2012 to travel with her husband. They live and work full time in a 40' travel trailer with their little dog Bingo. Besides writing romance novels, she enjoys selling art on Etsy and spoiling their three grandchildren. <br /><br />As a writer, Kirsten's goal is to create strong female characters who face challenging, painful, and sometimes comical situations. She believes that the best way to deal with struggle is through friendship and women helping women. She knows good stories are based on interesting and relatable characters.</span>
